        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.9b09703"><meta property="og:title" content="Anatase TiO2 as a Na+-Storage Anode Active Material for Dual-Ion Batteries"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/acsami.9b09703.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Anatase TiO2 used as the sodium-storage anode is coupled with a graphite cathode to construct dual-ion batteries. The batteries display wide voltage window (1.0–4.7 V), long cycling stability (98 mAh g–1 after 1400 cycles at 500 mA g–1), and considerable rate performance (102 mAh g–1 at 1500 mA g–1). Furthermore, the kinetic behaviors of Na+ and PF6– ions are investigated through electrochemical impedance spectroscopy, the galvanostatic intermittent titration technique, and the potentiostatic intermittent titration technique. The corresponding apparent ion diffusion coefficient is calculated, and the results indicate that the transport of PF6– anions in the graphite cathode is swift."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/acsami.9b09703.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/1122814~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="931889c22ede54b8-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="931889c22ede54b8-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: 'f08a7453-7652-4cf5-a518-3b7eb33f3f1e'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

src="/specs/products/achs/releasedAssets/public/mathjax-0a9852ad89643b94fe5099b753f6a294/MathJax.js?config=TeX-AMS-MML_HTMLorMML"></script><script type="text/x-mathjax-config;executed=true">MathJax.Hub.Config({
            menuSettings: {
                zoom: "Click",
                zscale: "150%"
            },
            SVG: {
                fonts: ["STIX-Web"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
            },
            "HTML-CSS": {
                fonts: ["STIX"],
                linebreaks: { automatic: true },
                scale: 90,
            },
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("mml Jax Ready", function () {
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            MML.mi.prototype.setTeXclass = function (prev) {
                this.getPrevClass(prev);
                return this;
            };
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                setTeXclass: function (prev) {
                    this.getPrevClass(prev);
                    for (var i = 0, m = this.data.length; i < m; i++) {
                        if (this.data[i]) this.data[i].setTeXclass();
                    }
                    return this;
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("SVG Jax Ready", function () {
            var FONT = MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"] || MathJax.OutputJax.SVG.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"];
            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("MathML Jax Ready", function () {
            var PARSE = MathJax.InputJax.MathML.Parse;
            var ADD = PARSE.prototype.AddChildren;
            PARSE.Augment({
                AddChildren: function (mml, node) {
                    ADD.call(this, mml, node);
                    if (mml.type === 'mrow') {
                        var first = mml.data[0], last = mml.data[mml.data.length-1];
                        if (mml.open && !mml.data[0].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.open;
                        if (mml.close && !mml.data[mml.data.length - 1].Get('stretchy')) delete mml.close;
                    }
                }
            });
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS Jax Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax['HTML-CSS'];
            var DELIMITERS = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.DELIMITERS;
            var FONT = HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-variant"] || HTMLCSS.FONTDATA.VARIANT["-STIX-Web-variant"]

            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;

            MML.mrow.Augment({
              _HTMLlineBreaks: MML.mrow.prototype.HTMLlineBreaks,
              HTMLlineBreaks: function (span) {

                if (this.parent.linebreakContainer && this.Get("display") === "inline") return false;
                return this._HTMLlineBreaks(span);
              }
            });


            DELIMITERS[0x0305] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x00AF};
            DELIMITERS[0x033F] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x003D};
            DELIMITERS[0x20E1] = {dir: "H", alias: 0x2194};

            if (FONT) {
                FONT.remap[0xB0]= [0x25E6, "normal"];
                FONT.remap[0x2A]= [0x2217, "normal"];
            }

            delete MathJax.ElementJax.mml.mo.prototype.remapChars['°'];
        });

        MathJax.Hub.Register.StartupHook("HTML-CSS multiline Ready", function () {
            var HTMLCSS = MathJax.OutputJax["HTML-CSS"];
            var MML = MathJax.ElementJax.mml;
            var PENALTY = MML.mbase.prototype.HTMLlinebreakPenalty;

            MML.msqrt.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mroot.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mfrac.Augment({
                linebreakContainer: false,
                HTMLbetterBreak: function () {return false}
            });
            MML.mspace.Augment({
                defaultDef: {
                    indentalign: MML.INDENTALIGN.AUTO,
                    indentshift: "0",
                    indenttarget: "",
                    indentalignfirst: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftfirst: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT,
                    indentalignlast: MML.INDENTALIGN.INDENTALIGN,
                    indentshiftlast: MML.INDENTSHIFT.INDENTSHIFT
                },
                HTMLbetterBreak: function (info,state) {
                    if (info.values && info.values.id === this.spanID) {return false}
                    var values = this.getValues(
                        "linebreak",
                        "indentalign","indentshift",
                        "indentalignfirst","indentshiftfirst",
                        "indentalignlast","indentshiftlast"
                    );
                    var linebreakValue = values.linebreak;
                    if (!linebreakValue || this.hasDimAttr()) {
                        linebreakValue = MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO;
                    }
                    var W = info.scanW, span = this.HTMLspanElement(), w = span.bbox.w;
                    if (span.style.paddingLeft) {w += HTMLCSS.unEm(span.style.paddingLeft)}
                    if (W - info.shift === 0) {return false} // don't break at zero width
                    var offset = HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth - W;

                    if (state.n === 0 && (values.indentshiftfirst !== state.VALUES.indentshiftfirst ||
                        values.indentalignfirst !== state.VALUES.indentalignfirst)) {
                        var align = this.HTMLgetAlign(state,values),
                            shift = this.HTMLgetShift(state,values,align);
                        offset += (info.shift - shift);
                    }

                    var penalty = Math.floor(offset / HTMLCSS.linebreakWidth * 1000);
                    if (penalty < 0) {penalty = PENALTY.toobig - 3*penalty}
                    penalty += info.nest * PENALTY.nestfactor;

                    var linebreak = PENALTY[linebreakValue]||0;
                    if (linebreakValue === MML.LINEBREAK.AUTO && w >= PENALTY.spacelimit &&
                        !this.mathbackground && !this.background)
                    {linebreak = [(w+PENALTY.spaceoffset)*PENALTY.spacefactor]}
                    if (!MathJax.Object.isArray(linebreak)) {
                        if (linebreak || offset >= 0) {penalty = linebreak * info.nest}
                    } else {penalty = Math.max(1,penalty + linebreak[0] * info.nest)}

                    if (penalty >= info.penalty) {return false}
                    info.penalty = penalty; info.values = values; info.W = W; info.w = w;
                    values.lineleading = state.VALUES.lineleading;
                    values.linebreakstyle = "before"; values.id = this.spanID;
                    return true;
                }
            });


            
            PENALTY.goodbreak = [-400];

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="931889c22ede54b8-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

<script nonce="931889c22ede54b8-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Anatase TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; as a Na&lt;sup&gt;+&lt;/sup&gt;-Storage Anode Active Material for Dual-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b09703", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Anatase TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; as a Na&lt;sup&gt;+&lt;/sup&gt;-Storage Anode Active Material for Dual-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b09703", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Anatase TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; as a Na&lt;sup&gt;+&lt;/sup&gt;-Storage Anode Active Material for Dual-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b09703", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Anatase TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; as a Na&lt;sup&gt;+&lt;/sup&gt;-Storage Anode Active Material for Dual-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b09703", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Anatase TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; as a Na&lt;sup&gt;+&lt;/sup&gt;-Storage Anode Active Material for Dual-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b09703", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Anatase TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; as a Na&lt;sup&gt;+&lt;/sup&gt;-Storage Anode Active Material for Dual-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b09703", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Anatase TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; as a Na&lt;sup&gt;+&lt;/sup&gt;-Storage Anode Active Material for Dual-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b09703", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Anatase TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; as a Na&lt;sup&gt;+&lt;/sup&gt;-Storage Anode Active Material for Dual-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b09703", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "Anatase TiO&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt; as a Na&lt;sup&gt;+&lt;/sup&gt;-Storage Anode Active Material for Dual-Ion Batteries", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.9b09703", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});
</script>

        </div></div><div class="article__pubdate"><span>Research Article</span><time datetime="2019-07-29">July 29, 2019</time></div><h1 class="article_header-title" tabindex="0"><span class="hlFld-Title" property="headline">Anatase TiO<sub>2</sub> as a Na<sup>+</sup>-Storage Anode Active Material for Dual-Ion Batteries</span><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy article link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Article link copied!</span></div></h1><ul class="loa"><li><span><span class="hlFld-ContribAuthor" tabindex="0" data-id="article_author_info" property="author">Xiaohong data-db-target-of="aboutArticleMetrics" id="about-article-metrics" class="dropBlock__holder"><button class="articleMetrics_close"> <i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-close_thin"></i><span The batteries display wide voltage window (1.0–4.7 V), long cycling stability (98 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 1400 cycles at 500 mA g<sup>–1</sup>), and considerable rate performance (102 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 1500 mA g<sup>–1</sup>). Furthermore, the kinetic behaviors of Na<sup>+</sup> and PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> ions are investigated through electrochemical impedance spectroscopy, the galvanostatic intermittent titration technique, and the potentiostatic intermittent titration technique. The corresponding apparent ion diffusion coefficient is calculated, and the results indicate that the transport of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> anions in the graphite cathode is swift.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D30453%26pageCount%3D7%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DXiaohong%2BWang%252C%2BLi%2BQi%252C%2BHongyu%2BWang%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D11%26issueNum%3D33%26contentID%3Dacsami.9b09703%26title%3DAnatase%2BTiO2%2Bas%2Ba%2BNa%252B-Storage%2BAnode%2BActive%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BDual-Ion%2BBatteries%26numPages%3D7%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D30459%26publicationDate%3DAugust%2B2019" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright © 2019 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">
                                        Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291442&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Anode materials"> Anode materials </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291337&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Carbon"> Carbon </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes"> Electrodes </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290667&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Ions"> Ions </a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290689&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Oxides"> Oxides </a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article__tags article__tags--keywords hlFld-Abstract"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Anatase+Tio2&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_anatase%20TiO2">anatase TiO<sub>2</sub></a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Dual-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_dual-ion%20batteries">dual-ion batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Kinetic+Behaviors&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_kinetic%20behaviors">kinetic behaviors</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Diffusion+Coefficient&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_diffusion%20coefficient">diffusion coefficient</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Na%2B-storage+Anode&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_Na%2B-storage%20anode">Na<sup>+</sup>-storage anode</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody" style="width: 384px;"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">Nowadays, the limited and unevenly distributed lithium sources are incapable of satisfying the ever-increasing requirement in electrochemical energy devices. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4" aria-label="reference 1 to 4">(1−4)</a> In the postlithium battery generation, a dual-ion battery (DIB) fabricated with a graphite cathode and a Na<sup>+</sup>-storage anode provides a promising alternative. Sodium-based DIBs display considerable electrochemical performance, such as the high output voltage, acceptable energy density, long cycle life, and so on. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref5 ref6 ref7 ref8 ref9 ref10" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref5 ref6 ref7 ref8 ref9 ref10" aria-label="reference 5 to 10">(5−10)</a> Furthermore, graphite without a transition metal is ecofriendly and the processing technology is mature. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref11 ref12" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref11 ref12" aria-label="reference 11 and 12">(11,12)</a> The sodium-based organic solvent taken as the electrolyte makes DIBs free of lithium.</div><div class="NLM_p">At present, Na<sup>+</sup>-storage materials in DIBs only include carbon, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref13 ref14 ref15 ref16 ref17" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref13 ref14 ref15 ref16 ref17" aria-label="reference 13 to 17">(13−17)</a> MoS<sub>2</sub>/carbon, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18 ref19 ref20 ref21" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref18 ref19 ref20 ref21" aria-label="reference 18 to 21">(18−21)</a> FePO<sub>4</sub>, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref22" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref22" aria-label="reference 22">(22)</a> Sn, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23 ref24" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref23 ref24" aria-label="reference 23 and 24">(23,24)</a> and Na<sub>2</sub>Ti<sub>3</sub>O<sub>7</sub>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref25 ref26" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref25 ref26" aria-label="reference 25 and 26">(25,26)</a> The development of DIBs suffers from the lack of suitable anode active material. Graphite fails to form a stable intercalation compound in ester-based electrolytes. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27 ref28" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref27 ref28" aria-label="reference 27 and 28">(27,28)</a> Graphitic carbon and hard carbon are subjected to the intercalation plateau around 0.1 V, causing the growth of sodium dendrite. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref29" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref29" aria-label="reference 29">(29)</a> Alloys and metal oxides have to undergo drastic volume changes during sodiation/desodiation. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref30" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref30" aria-label="reference 30">(30)</a> Titanium dioxide (TiO<sub>2</sub>) is identified as a promising Na<sup>+</sup>-storage anode due to its high safety, low cost, and stable structure. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref31 ref32" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref31 ref32" aria-label="reference 31 and 32">(31,32)</a> In addition, the appropriate sodiation potential (∼0.8 V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>) avoids the sodium metal deposition. Thapa et al. have utilized TiO<sub>2</sub> as a Li<sup>+</sup>-storage anode for DIBs in 2010, and TiO<sub>2</sub>/graphite lithium-based DIBs have displayed 91 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with the retention of 94.5% after 30 cycles, which demonstrates that the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode can cooperate with the graphite cathode well. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref33" aria-label="reference 33">(33)</a> In theory, TiO<sub>2</sub> can be applied as a Na<sup>+</sup>-storage anode for DIBs.</div><div class="NLM_p last">In this study, anatase TiO<sub>2</sub> is involved as the Na<sup>+</sup>-storage anode for DIBs for the first time ever. TiO<sub>2</sub>/graphite DIBs exhibit high output voltage, long cycle life, and superior capacity. Moreover, the kinetic behaviors of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> in the graphite cathode and Na<sup>+</sup> in the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode are investigated by electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS), the galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT), and the potentiostatic intermittent titration technique (PITT).</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i3">Experimental Section</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The morphology of anatase TiO<sub>2</sub> (99.8%, Aladdin Chemistry Co., Ltd.) was verified by transmission electron microscopy (TEM) images with a JEM-2100F microscope operated at 200 kV. The X-ray diffraction (XRD) pattern was characterized by a Bruker D8 advance diffractometer with Cu Kα radiation (λ = 1.5418 Å). The specific area was obtained from the Brunauer–Emmett–Teller (BET) method, and the pore size distribution was analyzed using the nonlinear density functional theory (NLDFT) model.</div><div class="NLM_p last">Anatase TiO<sub>2</sub> (without further treatment) was mixed with carboxymethyl cellulose (M.W. 700 000, Aladdin Chemistry Co., Ltd.) and super-p carbon black at a mass ratio of 80:10:10 in water to form a homogeneous slurry. The slurry was coated on the copper foil and cut into a round disk (ϕ = 14 mm) to attain the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode (∼1.5 mg per electrode). The mixture of graphite KS-6 (Imerys Co., Ltd., Switzerland) and teflonized acetylene black (Denka Co. Ltd.) (2:1 by weight) was pressed on aluminum mesh to obtain the graphite cathode. The mass ratio of graphite and TiO<sub>2</sub> is 3. The electrolyte was 1 M NaPF<sub>6</sub> dissolved in the mixture of ethylene carbonate and ethyl methyl carbonate (1:2 by volume). All of the batteries were assembled in a glovebox full of Ar (H<sub>2</sub>O, O<sub>2</sub> &lt; 1 ppm) after all electrodes were dried at 130 °C in vacuum for 3 h. The cyclic voltammetric (CV) curves, EIS, and PITT tests were conducted in a CHI600C electrochemical workstation. The graphite or TiO<sub>2</sub> electrode served as the working electrode, and sodium metal worked as the reference electrode and counter electrode. The galvanostatic charge–discharge test, rate test, and GITT experiments of batteries were conducted using a Land 2001A cell test system. The current density and specific capacity were all based on the mass of the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode in the text. Before EIS, GITT, and PITT experiments, the graphite cathode and TiO<sub>2</sub> anode with sodium-ion batteries worked for five cycles at the current density of 50 mA g<sup>–1</sup> in the voltage ranges of 3.0–5.0 and 0–3.0 V, respectively.</div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i4">Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The particles of TiO<sub>2</sub> show a rod-like shape, and the size is 25 nm (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>a). The XRD pattern can be indexed to the anatase phase (JCPDS no. 21-1272) (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>b). The BET specific surface area is 121.27 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>–1</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>c), and the average pore diameter is 6.08 nm as analyzed by the NLDFT model (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>d).</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/medium/am9b09703_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/large/am9b09703_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. Physical properties of TiO<sub>2</sub>. (a) TEM image, (b) XRD pattern, (c) N<sub>2</sub> adsorption/desorption isotherms, and (d) pore distribution.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/large/am9b09703_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b09703&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The Na<sup>+</sup> ion-storage ability of TiO<sub>2</sub> is evaluated through the galvanostatic charge/discharge test (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/suppl_file/am9b09703_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>). The initial capacities are 233 and 109 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with the initial Coulombic efficiency (ICE) of 46.9%. The recent review about the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode for sodium-ion batteries describes the ICE ranges from 20 to 50% in general. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref32" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref32" aria-label="reference 32">(32)</a> The irreversible capacity loss in the first cycle stems from the formation of solid electrolyte interface (SEI) film, some side reactions of the electrolyte, the sluggish Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion, and the initial structural reorganization. After 150 cycles, the reversible capacity is 118 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>. To ensure that the active sites of TiO<sub>2</sub> are occupied eventually, there ought to be excess graphite. Based on the previous study, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref16 ref17" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref16 ref17" aria-label="reference 16 and 17">(16,17)</a> the mass of graphite is three times higher than that of TiO<sub>2</sub>. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>a represents the charge–discharge curves of DIBs in the potential window of 1.0–4.7 V and the current density of 500 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. There is an obvious couple of plateaus in 3.5 V. A unique plateau at ∼4.5 V is found in the first and second typical charge curves, which is distinct from the subsequent cycles. The charge platform (∼4.5 V) of DIBs is mainly caused by the discharge platform of the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode at ∼0 V (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/suppl_file/am9b09703_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S1</a>a). In the 1400th cycle, a charge plateau is at ∼3.8 V (above 3.5 V), owing to the polarization of DIBs. The initial capacities is 146 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> (charge) and 123 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> (discharge) with the ICE of 84.7%. The capacity increases during the first 50 cycles due to the activation process, and the reversible capacity at the 50th cycle is 140 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>. After 1400 cycles, the specific capacity is 98 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> with the retention of 70% (vs the capacity of the 50th cycle) (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>b) and the rate of decline in capacity is merely 0.022% per cycle. The cyclic stability of TiO<sub>2</sub>/graphite DIBs is found to be superior to common sodium-based DIBs. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref15 ref19 ref20 ref22" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref15 ref19 ref20 ref22" aria-label="reference 15, 19, 20 and 22">(15,19,20,22)</a> The gradual decay may be attributed to the mismatched transport of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> and Na<sup>+</sup> ions. The rate performance is described in <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>c,d. The discharge capacity is 102 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at the current density of 1500 mA g<sup>–1</sup>. Moreover, the plateaus are around 3.5 V without an obvious shift at diverse current densities, which suggests the small polarization in DIBs. The energy and power densities of DIBs are estimated based on the mass of TiO<sub>2</sub> and graphite. TiO<sub>2</sub>/graphite DIBs deliver the energy density of 113 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup> at the power density of 41.75 W kg<sup>–1</sup> and 74 Wh kg<sup>–1</sup> at 1121 W kg<sup>–1</sup> (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/suppl_file/am9b09703_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S2</a>).</div><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/medium/am9b09703_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/large/am9b09703_0002.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. Electrochemical performance of TiO<sub>2</sub>/graphite sodium-based DIBs. (a) Typical charge–discharge curves and (b) capacities and Coulombic efficiencies vs cycle number at 500 mA g<sup>–1</sup> in 1.0–4.7 V. (c) Typical charge–discharge curves and (d) capacities and Coulombic efficiencies vs cycle number at various current densities in 1.0–4.7 V.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/large/am9b09703_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b09703&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">To gain understanding of the respective electrochemical reaction in negative and positive electrodes, we trace the separate potentials vs active carbon (AC) quasi-reference electrode in the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode and graphite cathode during DIB operation (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref34" aria-label="reference 34">(34)</a> There are a couple of plateaus near 3.5 V controlled by the plateaus of the graphite cathode (1.7 V vs AC) and the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode (−1.8 V vs AC). The potential variations of the graphite cathode and TiO<sub>2</sub> anode gradually stabilize. In the fifth cycle, the TiO<sub>2</sub>/graphite DIB cycles between 1.0 and 4.7 V at the current density of 500 mA g<sup>–1</sup>, the graphite cathode between 1.18 and 2.15 V vs AC (i.e., 3.88–4.85 V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>), and TiO<sub>2</sub> between −2.55 and 0.24 V vs AC (i.e., 0.15–2.94 V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>). In the region, the electrolyte does not decompose violently and the electrode can maintain stability, which ensures the stability of DIBs.</div><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/medium/am9b09703_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/large/am9b09703_0003.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. Potential profiles of the graphite cathode and TiO<sub>2</sub> anode vs the AC quasi-reference electrode in the TiO<sub>2</sub>/graphite DIBs with the current density of 500 mA g<sup>–1</sup> and the voltage range of 1.0–4.7 V.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/large/am9b09703_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b09703&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Kinetic behaviors of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> anions and Na<sup>+</sup> cations are also significant influencing factors in DIB electrochemical performance. EIS plots for the graphite cathode and TiO<sub>2</sub> anode are measured in the frequency range from 100 kHz to 10 mHz with sodium-ion batteries (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>a). The two impedance curves show semicircles in the high-to-medium frequency, which are attributed to the SEI film resistance (<i>R</i><sub>f</sub>) and the charge-transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>). The fitting results reveal that <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of Na<sup>+</sup> cations in the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode (4829 Ω) is larger than that of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> anions in the graphite cathode (209.48 Ω) (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/suppl_file/am9b09703_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S1</a>), indicating slower charge-transfer kinetics of Na<sup>+</sup> ions. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref35" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref35" aria-label="reference 35">(35)</a> The slope line in the low-frequency region is attributed to the Warburg impedance, depicting the diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup> and PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> ions in the electrode materials, which can be used to calculate the ion diffusion coefficient (<i>D</i>) by equation <i>D</i> = <i>R</i><sup>2</sup><i>T</i><sup>2</sup>/2<i>A</i><sup>2</sup><i>n</i><sup>4</sup><i>F</i><sup>4</sup><i>C</i><sup>2</sup>σ<sup>2</sup>, <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36 ref37 ref38 ref39" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref36 ref37 ref38 ref39" aria-label="reference 36 to 39">(36−39)</a> where <i>R</i> is the gas constant (8.314 J mol<sup>–1</sup> K<sup>–1</sup>), <i>T</i> is the absolute temperature (298.15 K), <i>A</i> is the geometric area of the electrode (1.54 cm<sup>2</sup>), <i>n</i> is the number of electrons transferred per molecule in the electrochemical reaction, <i>F</i> is the Faraday constant (96 500 C mol<sup>–1</sup>), <i>C</i> is the concentration of ions, and σ is the Warburg factor. <i>C</i> is calculated from the tap density (ρ) and the molecular weight (<i>M</i>) (<i>C</i> = <i>n</i>/<i>V</i> = (<i>m</i>/<i>M</i>)/<i>V</i> = (ρ<i>V</i>/<i>M</i>)/<i>V</i> = ρ/<i>M</i>). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref40" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref40" aria-label="reference 40">(40)</a> The tap densities of graphite and TiO<sub>2</sub> are 0.194 and 0.378 g cm<sup>–3</sup>, respectively. σ is obtained from the linear slope of <i>Z</i><sub>re</sub> vs ω<sup>–1/2</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>b). <i>D</i> of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> ions in the graphite cathode is 7.74 × 10<sup>–14</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup> and of Na<sup>+</sup> ions in the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode is 7.6 × 10<sup>–15</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup>. Comparing the values of <i>D</i>, the transport of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> anions in the graphite cathode is easier than that of Na<sup>+</sup> cations in the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode.</div><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/medium/am9b09703_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/large/am9b09703_0004.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. (a) EIS plots of the graphite cathode and TiO<sub>2</sub> anode at frequencies from 100 kHz to 10 mHz at 298.15 K. The insets are the magnified semicircle parts and the equivalent circuit model, respectively. (b) Real part <i>Z</i><sub>re</sub> of the complex impedance vs ω<sup>–1/2</sup>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/large/am9b09703_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b09703&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">In addition, GITT is also adopted to evaluate the kinetic behaviors of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> and Na<sup>+</sup> ions. <a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>a describes the schematic diagram of GITT, and <i>D</i> is calculated using the following equation. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41 ref42 ref43" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref41 ref42 ref43" aria-label="reference 41 to 43">(41−43)</a><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="ueq1"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/medium/am9b09703_m001.gif" alt="" id="_i5"></div><div class="label"></div></div></span>Here, τ is the duration of the current pulse,&nbsp;<i>M</i><sub>B</sub> is the molar weight, <i>S</i> is the geometric area of the electrode, <i>m</i><sub>B</sub> is the active material mass, and <i>V</i><sub>M</sub> is defined as the molecular volume. The lattice constants of graphite KS-6 are determined to be <i>a</i> = 2.456 Å, <i>b</i> = 2.456 Å, and <i>c</i> = 6.696 Å, and <i>V</i><sub>M</sub> is calculated to be 5.264 cm<sup>3</sup> mol<sup>–1</sup>. For anatase TiO<sub>2</sub>, the lattice constants are <i>a</i> = 3.785 Å, <i>b</i> = 3.785 Å, <i>c</i> = 9.514 Å, and <i>V</i><sub>M</sub> is 20.51 cm<sup>3</sup> mol<sup>–1</sup>. Δ<i>E</i><sub>s</sub> is the steady-state voltage change, and <i>E</i><sub>τ</sub> is the transient voltage during the titration process. In the GITT experiment, the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode is discharged from the open-circuit voltage (OCV) to 0.11 V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup> and the graphite cathode is charged from OCV to 4.85 V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup> by a series of intermittent current (50 mA g<sup>–1</sup>) for 30 min and then kept still at the open circuit for 10 h (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/suppl_file/am9b09703_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3</a>a,b). The selection of voltage range is based on potential files (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>). <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/suppl_file/am9b09703_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S3</a>c, d reveals the relationship between <i>E</i><sub>τ</sub> and τ<sup>1/2</sup> during a single titration process for the graphite cathode and TiO<sub>2</sub> anode, respectively. Regarding the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode, <i>E</i><sub>τ</sub> has a linear relation with τ<sup>1/2</sup> and there is a deviation from the linear dependence referring to the graphite cathode. The deviation may be attributed to the high coefficient of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> ions, the increase of the graphite layer spacing, and the diffusion of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> ions occurring between graphite and graphite intercalation compounds. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref44 ref45 ref46 ref47 ref48" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref44 ref45 ref46 ref47 ref48" aria-label="reference 44 to 48">(44−48)</a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>b describes <i>D</i> of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> and Na<sup>+</sup> ions. For Na<sup>+</sup> cations in TiO<sub>2</sub>, the maximum value of <i>D</i> is 2.77 × 10<sup>–11</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup> (1.23 V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>) and the minimum value is 1.79 × 10<sup>–12</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup> (0.11 V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>). In the case of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> ions in graphite, the value of <i>D</i> is within the range of 2.24 × 10<sup>–12</sup> to 3.17 × 10<sup>–10</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup>. <i>D</i> of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> anions is larger than that of Na<sup>+</sup> cations at the corresponding voltage, implying that the transport of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> ions in the graphite cathode is more facile.</div><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/medium/am9b09703_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/large/am9b09703_0005.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. (a) Schematic diagram of the GITT method. (b) <i>D</i> of Na<sup>+</sup> and PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> ions calculated from the GITT curves as a function of the voltage for the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode and graphite cathode, respectively. The TiO<sub>2</sub> anode is discharged from OCV to 0.11 V, and the graphite cathode is charged from OCV to 4.85 V.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/large/am9b09703_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b09703&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">PITT is also performed to calculate <i>D</i> of Na<sup>+</sup> and PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> ions. The TiO<sub>2</sub> anode is discharged from 2.05 (OCV) to 0.15 V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>, while the graphite cathode is charged from 4.15 to 4.85 V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>. The potential difference for each step is Δ<i>E</i> = 0.05 V, and the time span is 1200 s. <i>D</i> is calculated by the following equation. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref49 ref50 ref51" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref49 ref50 ref51" aria-label="reference 49 to 51">(49−51)</a><span class="NLM_disp-formula"><div class="MathJaxEquation" id="ueq2"><div class="equation"><img class="imgWithoutFigViewer " src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/medium/am9b09703_m002.gif" alt="" id="_i6"></div><div class="label"></div></div></span><i>i</i> is the step current, <i>L</i> is the diffusion distance, and <i>t</i> is the step time. <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/suppl_file/am9b09703_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figures S4</a> and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/suppl_file/am9b09703_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S5</a> depict the chronoamperometry and ln(<i>i</i>) – <i>t</i> curves of the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode and graphite cathode, respectively. <i>D</i> of Na<sup>+</sup> cations ranges from 9.206 × 10<sup>–10</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup> (2.0 V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>) to 4.718 × 10<sup>–9</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup> (0.65 V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>), and <i>D</i> of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> anions changes from 1.813 × 10<sup>–9</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup> (4.15 V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>) to 4.38 × 10<sup>–7</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup> (4.85 V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>) (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>). At the corresponding voltage, <i>D</i> of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> anions in the graphite cathode is larger.</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/medium/am9b09703_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/large/am9b09703_0006.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. <i>D</i> of Na<sup>+</sup> and PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> ions calculated from PITT curves as a function of the step voltage for TiO<sub>2</sub> and graphite electrodes, respectively (voltage range: TiO<sub>2</sub> anode, 2.05–0.15 V; graphite cathode, 4.15–4.85 V).</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/large/am9b09703_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b09703&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p"><i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> and <i>D</i><sub>PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup></sub> are both in the reasonable domain compared with the reported literature (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/suppl_file/am9b09703_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Table S2</a>). The results of EIS, GITT, and PITT are consistent. <i>D</i> of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> is larger than that of Na<sup>+</sup>. The transport of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> is faster, while the ionic radius of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> anions is bigger than that of Na<sup>+</sup> cations. It is supposed that the ionic radius is not the decisive factor based on the Arrhenius equation <i>k</i> = <i>A</i> exp(−<i>E</i><sub>a</sub>/<i>k</i><sub>B</sub><i>T</i>). <i>k</i> is the reaction rate constant, which can represent <i>D</i>. <i>A</i> is the preexponential factor and is treated as an identical constant for PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> and Na<sup>+</sup> ions. <i>E</i><sub>a</sub> is the activation energy, <i>k</i><sub>B</sub> is the Boltzmann constant, and <i>T</i> is the absolute temperature. The energy barrier of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> ion diffusion along the (100) direction of graphite is 0.23 eV and the migration energy barrier of Na<sup>+</sup> ions in anatase TiO<sub>2</sub> is 0.56 eV, which are both obtained by the density functional theory (DFT). <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref52 ref53" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref52 ref53" aria-label="reference 52 and 53">(52,53)</a> According to the Arrhenius equation, the ratio of <i>D</i><sub>PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup></sub> and <i>D</i><sub>Na<sup>+</sup></sub> is 3.7 × 10<sup>5</sup>. However, the ratios measured by EIS, GITT, and PITT are found to be far less than the theoretical value. Actually, the values of <i>A</i> for PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> and Na<sup>+</sup> ions should not be equal. <i>A</i> is determined by the nature of the reaction and is independent of the temperature and the concentration. The ionic radius, morphology, and other physical properties may affect the value of <i>A</i>. The difference in <i>A</i> reduces the rate gap between PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> and Na<sup>+</sup> ions.</div><div class="NLM_p">Furthermore, the CV curves tested at varying scan rates shed light on the Na<sup>+</sup>-storage manner in the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode to account for the sluggish kinetic behavior (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>a–d). The relationship between the peak current (<i>i</i><sub>p</sub>) and the scan rate (<i>v</i>) can be described with the power law formula, <i>i</i><sub>p</sub> = <i>av</i><sup>b</sup>. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref54 ref55 ref56 ref57" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref54 ref55 ref56 ref57" aria-label="reference 54 to 57">(54−57)</a> Both <i>a</i> and <i>b</i> are constants. Parameter <i>b</i> can be obtained from the slope of the line log(<i>i</i><sub>p</sub>) – log(<i>v</i>) (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>e). The 0.5 value of <i>b</i> indicates a diffusion-controlled intercalation process and 1 represents a capacitive process. For the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode, <i>b</i> is 0.79 below 10 mV s<sup>–1</sup> and 0.48 above 10 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. There is a distinct transformation in the Na<sup>+</sup>-storage mechanism of the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode, which changes from a capacitive process to diffusion-controlled intercalation. However, when TiO<sub>2</sub> is used as the Li<sup>+</sup>-storage anode, CV curves are described in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/suppl_file/am9b09703_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6</a>a–d and the value of <i>b</i> is 0.57 (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/suppl_file/am9b09703_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">Figure S6</a>e). The Li<sup>+</sup>-storage manner is diffusion-controlled intercalation, which is different from the Na<sup>+</sup>-storage mechanism. <i>D</i> can be calculated by the Randles–Sevick equation <i>i</i><sub>p</sub> = 2.69 × 10<sup>5</sup><i>Z</i><sup>3/2</sup><i>AD</i><sup>1/2</sup><i>Cv</i><sup>1/2</sup>, where <i>Z</i>, <i>A</i>, and <i>C</i> is the charge-transfer number, the geometric electrode area, and the concentration of Na<sup>+</sup> (or Li<sup>+</sup>) ions, respectively. <a href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref58 ref59" id="referenceLink" data-rid="ref58 ref59" aria-label="reference 58 and 59">(58,59)</a> When <i>Z</i>, <i>A</i>, and <i>C</i> have the same values for Na<sup>+</sup> and Li<sup>+</sup> ions in anatase TiO<sub>2</sub>, <i>D</i> can be obtained by the slope of the line <i>i</i><sub>p</sub> – <i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup> (<a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">Figures </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>f and <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/suppl_file/am9b09703_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">S6</a>f). The slope of the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode in the lithium-ion battery is 0.0916, and the slope of the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode in the sodium-ion battery changes from 0.0609 to 0.0559 with the increase in the scan rate. <i>D</i> of Li<sup>+</sup> ions is larger than that of Na<sup>+</sup> ions due to the smaller radius of Li<sup>+</sup> ions. The transport of Na<sup>+</sup> ions slows down when the scan rate exceeds 10 mV s<sup>–1</sup>, which is ascribed to the variation of the Na<sup>+</sup>-storage mechanism.</div><figure id="fig7" data-index="7" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 7</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/medium/am9b09703_0007.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/large/am9b09703_0007.jpeg" id="gr7" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 7. (a–d) CV curves of the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode with sodium-ion batteries at various scan rates. The relationship between (e) log(<i>i</i><sub>p</sub>) and log(<i>v</i>) and (f) <i>i</i><sub>p</sub> and <i>v</i><sup>1/2</sup>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/asset/images/large/am9b09703_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.9b09703&amp;id=fig7"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i7">Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">The TiO<sub>2</sub>/graphite sodium-based dual-ion battery exhibits high output voltage (4.7 V), long cyclic life (1400 cycles with the specific capacity of 98 mAh g<sup>–1</sup>), and outstanding rate performance (102 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 1500 mA g<sup>–1</sup>). Furthermore, the behaviors of positive and negative electrodes are investigated. The graphite cathode and TiO<sub>2</sub> anode cycle in the voltage ranges of 3.88–4.85 V and 0.15–2.94 V vs Na/Na<sup>+</sup>, respectively, which ensures the stability of DIBs. The ion diffusion coefficient is calculated by EIS, GITT, and PITT. All of the results are consistent and indicate that the transport of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>–</sup> is quicker than that of Na<sup>+</sup> ions. For the purpose of satisfactory DIBs, increasing the Na<sup>+</sup> ion diffusion rate in the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode is supposed to be an available approach.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i8">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.9b09703" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.9b09703</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Na<sup>+</sup>-storage ability of the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode; Ragone plot of TiO<sub>2</sub>/graphite DIBs; GITT curves; chronoamperometry plots and the relationship of ln(<i>i</i>) and <i>t</i>; CV curves of TiO<sub>2</sub> with Li-ion batteries; table for fitting results of Nyqusit plots; and reference table for diffusion coefficient (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/suppl_file/am9b09703_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/suppl_file/am9b09703_si_001.pdf">am9b09703_si_001.pdf (943.03 kb)</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.9b09703" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget" style="display: block;"></div><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="85b54935-30e9-4058-a6d2-0b40fb754a85" class="mb-4">

Energy Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">187008</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit4R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">4</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Perspective on Performance, Cost, and Technical Challenges for Practical Dual-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Placke, Tobias; Heckmann, Andreas; Schmuch, Richard; Meister, Paul; Beltrop, Kolja; Winter, Martin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Joule</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">12</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2528-2550</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Cell Press</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">While lithium-ion batteries dominate the field of high-energy-d. applications, a variety of promising alternative battery technologies exist that might be suitable for various application purposes.  Their requirements may vary considerably, e.g., for stationary batteries they are significantly different from those of traction batteries in elec. vehicles, i.e., low installation and lifetime cost and a long cycle life are the key parameters for the former ones.  Here, we review the recent developments of dual-ion battery (DIB) and particularly of dual-graphite battery technologies, which may be considered as sustainable option for grid storage.  We present the progress and challenges of DIB materials and electrolytes, esp. with respect to performance parameters, e.g., energy d. and cycling stability as well as cost.  We discuss the major challenges for practical application and critically evaluate the DIB technol. along with an assessment of the potential to fulfill the targets for grid storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref5" class="refNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit5" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2017.01.034"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meister, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fromm, O.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rothermel, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kasnatscheew, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Winter, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Placke, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium-Based vs. Lithium-Based Dual-Ion Cells: Electrochemical Study of Anion Intercalation/De-Intercalation into/from Graphite and Metal Plating/Dissolution Behavior</span>. <i>Electrochim.
