                        cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-Based vs. Lithium-Based Dual-Ion Cells: Electrochemical Study of Anion Intercalation/De-Intercalation into/from Graphite and Metal Plating/Dissolution Behavior</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Meister, Paul; Fromm, Olga; Rothermel, Sergej; Kasnatscheew, Johannes; Winter, Martin; Placke, Tobias</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">228</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">18-27</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy storage systems utilizing a simultaneous intercalation of anions into a graphite host structure at the pos. electrode and intercalation/insertion/redn. or deposition of cations at the neg. electrode during charge, were introduced under the term dual-ion cells, recently.  In this work, the electrochem. intercalation of TFSI- anions into graphite has been studied in sodium-based dual-ion cells (SDICs) at different upper cut-off potentials varying between 4.5-4.7 V vs. Na/Na+.  Electrochem. characteristics of SDICs, including the reversible capacity, Coulombic efficiency, energy efficiency and onset potentials for anion intercalation, were evaluated in comparison to the lithium-based dual-ions cells (LDICs).  A stable charge/discharge cycling performance over 500 cycles has been found for SDICs providing a specific capacity of ≈ 32 mAh g-1 and a Coulombic efficiency exceeding 99% at an upper cut-off potential of 4.7 V vs. Na/Na+ at the graphite cathode.  By the addn. of the electrolyte additive ethylene sulfite (ES), an increase of the reversible capacity to ≈ 46 mAh g-1 was achieved.  Furthermore, possible reasons for the overall inferior cycling performance in terms of capacity for SDICs as compared to LDICs such as an increased overpotential for plating/stripping of Na+ ions as compared to Li+ ions are discussed.  In this respect, it was also found that the addn. of ethylene sulfite particularly decreases the overpotentials for the metal plating process, which at least partially explains the enhanced reversible capacity in LDICs and SDICs by using ES as electrolyte additive.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref6" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2017.01.037"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Aladinli, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bordet, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ahlbrecht, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tübke, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Holzapfel, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Compositional Graphitic Cathode Investigation and Structural Characterization Tests for Na-Based Dual-Ion Battery Applications Using Ethylene Carbonate: Ethyl Methyl Carbonate-Based Electrolyte</span>. <i>Electrochim.                         cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Compositional graphitic cathode investigation and structural characterization tests for Na-based dual-ion battery applications using ethylene carbonate:ethyl methyl carbonate-based electrolyte</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Aladinli, Sinan; Bordet, Francois; Ahlbrecht, Katharina; Tuebke, Jens; Holzapfel, Michael</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As significant as the electrolyte selection is for dual-ion battery applications, the characteristics of the graphitic cathode can also be decisive for the resultant cell operation.  During this work, to find a promising electrode-electrolyte combination for Na-based dual-ion batteries, CCCV cycling tests were applied to different pos. electrode compns. to optimize the effects of carbon black and binder as well as to mitigate the irreversible charge losses, by utilizing 0.5 M NaPF6/EC:EMC electrolyte which was the most promising mixt. in our preceding study.  Electrodes consisting of 90% KS6 graphite, 2% carbon black and 8% binder was the most promising combination, and proved its superiority over SLP 30 type graphite, delivering 86.2 mAh/g discharge capacity by its lower particle size and larger surface area.  Moreover, structural characterization tests of Raman spectroscopy and x-ray diffraction were implemented by providing qual. and quant. insights to elucidate and characterize the PF-6 intercalation/de-intercalation characteristics for our Na-based dual-ion battery.  The results of the tests acknowledged that the surface and the bulk of the electrode behave differently.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref7" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2017.02.041"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Aladinli, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bordet, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ahlbrecht, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tübke, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Holzapfel, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Anion Intercalation into a Graphite Cathode from Various Sodium-Based Electrolyte Mixtures for Dual-Ion Battery Applications</span>. <i>Electrochim.                 10.1016/j.electacta.2017.02.041</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D231%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D468-478%26journal%3DElectrochim.%2BActa%26author%3DS.%2BAladinli%26author%3DF.%2BBordet%26author%3DK.%2BAhlbrecht%26author%3DJ.%2BT%25C3%25BCbke%26author%3DM.%2BHolzapfel%26title%3DAnion%2BIntercalation%2Binto%2Ba%2BGraphite%2BCathode%2Bfrom%2BVarious%2BSodium-Based%2BElectrolyte%2BMixtures%2Bfor%2BDual-Ion%2BBattery%2BApplications%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.electacta.2017.02.041&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b09703&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.electacta.2017.02.041&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anion intercalation into a graphite cathode from various sodium-based electrolyte mixtures for dual-ion battery applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Aladinli, Sinan; Bordet, Francois; Ahlbrecht, Katharina; Tuebke, Jens; Holzapfel, Michael</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrolyte plays a crucial role for dual-ion batteries by supplying the ions to be intercalated into electrodes.  Yet, high operation potentials of such batteries limit the no. of suitable electrolytes to be used since they have to be stable upon cycling.  Here, sodium-based electrolytes were investigated by applying stability and cycling tests in order to observe their influences on anion intercalation behavior using graphitic cathodes.  Intercalation of PF-6 anions with org. carbonate solvents revealed relatively better discharge capacities compared to its anionic counterparts and 0.5 M NaPF6/EC:EMC electrolyte was found to be the most promising mixt. among them.  PC solvent proved detrimental for anion intercalation, but FEC as an electrolyte additive in PC precluded undesired effects of PC and gave rise to reversible cycling.  However, the ionic liqs. based on TFSI- and FSI- anions, mostly, yielded capacity fading under a charging end potential of 5.0 V vs.  Na/Na+, except the 0.7 M NaTFSI/Pip14TFSI electrolyte, showing 98% coulombic efficiency over 200 cycles.  During this work, electrochem. tests were conducted and evaluated to comprehend the impacts of electrolytes on the anion intercalation process.  EC:EMC-based electrolyte was then used in our further research, where the compositional cathodic investigation was executed and the anion intercalation phenomenon was characterized.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref8" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1021/acs.jpcc.7b08429"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, H.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kao, Y.-T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">An, J.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, Y.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.-Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Freestanding Cathode Electrode Design for High-Performance Sodium Dual-Ion Battery</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Freestanding Cathode Electrode Design for High-Performance Sodium Dual-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liao, Hsiang-Ju; Chen, Yu-Mei; Kao, Yu-Ting; An, Ji-Yao; Lai, Ying-Huang; Wang, Di-Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">121</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, both advantages of sodium-ion batteries and dual-ion batteries have been combined in an innovated sodium-ion-based dual-ion battery (SDI) system using a Na metal film as anode and a freestanding meso-carbon microbead film (FS-MCMB) as cathode.  FS-MCMB in SDI battery exhibited a superior working performance with the specific capacity of 83.6 mAh/g and a remarkable long-term stability over 300 cycles.  The SDI battery with FS-MCMB exhibited an advantage of high mass d. loading in the range of 2-7.5 mg cm-2, which was equal to a comparable capacity of 78-83 mAh/g.  The electrochem. impedance anal. indicated that FS-MCMB provided a superior permeability, resulting in facilitating electrolyte infiltration into MCMB structure.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Dual-ion batteries operate on two intercalants: anions for the cathode and cations for the anode.  This battery was initially known as a dual-graphite battery, where both electrodes are graphitic carbon.  The primary challenge of dual-graphite batteries is the very high operation potential of the cathode, often requiring an upper cutoff potential above 5 V vs Li+/Li.  Such a potential readily oxidizes alkyl and alkylene carbonate-based electrolytes.  The anode side, in fact, can employ any anode of most metal-ion batteries, although, to date, the focus has still been the Li-graphite anode.  Recent progress has significantly advanced the technol. readiness level for this battery.  Additives or ionic liq. electrolytes help mitigate cathode irreversibility; nongraphite anodes, such as aluminum, allow new carbonate electrolytes that lack the necessity of ethylene carbonate; nongraphite cathodes, including metal-org. frameworks and polycyclic arom. hydrocarbons have exhibited a remarkable potential.  This Perspective highlights the challenges, summarizes the recent progress, and attempts to point out future directions in the field.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref12" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201700146"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Progress in Graphite Intercalation Compounds for Rechargeable Metal (Li, Na, K, Al)-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent Progress in Graphite Intercalation Compounds for Rechargeable Metal (Li, Na, K, Al)-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Xu Jiantie; Dou Yuhai; Liu Huakun; Dou Shixue; Wei Zengxi; Ma Jianmin; Deng Yonghong; Li Yutao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) with higher energy density are very necessary to meet the increasing demand for devices with better performance.  With the commercial success of lithiated graphite, other graphite intercalation compounds (GICs) have also been intensively reported, not only for LIBs, but also for other metal (Na, K, Al) ion batteries.  In this Progress Report, we briefly review the application of GICs as anodes and cathodes in metal (Li, Na, K, Al) ion batteries.  After a brief introduction on the development history of GICs, the electrochemistry of cationic GICs and anionic GICs is summarized.  We further briefly summarize the use of cationic GICs and anionic GICs in alkali ion batteries and the use of anionic GICs in aluminium-ion batteries.  Finally, we reach some conclusions on the drawbacks, major progress, emerging challenges, and some perspectives on the development of GICs for metal (Li, Na, K, Al) ion batteries.  Further development of GICs for metal (Li, Na, K, Al) ion batteries is not only a strong supplement to the commercialized success of lithiated-graphite for LIBs, but also an effective strategy to develop diverse high-energy batteries for stationary energy storage in the future.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref13" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b11824"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tao, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kang, Y.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mai, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.-X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">All Carbon Dual Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Dual ion batteries based on Na+ and PF6- received considerable attention due to their high operating voltage and the abundant Na resources.  Here, cheap and easily-obtained graphite that served as a cathode material for dual ion battery delivered a very high av. discharge platform (4.52 V vs. Na+/Na) using Na hexafluorophosphate in propylene carbonate (PC) as electrolyte.  The all-C dual ion batteries with graphite as cathode and hard C as anode exhibited an ultra-high discharge voltage of 4.3 V, and a reversible capacity of 62 mAh/g at 40 mA/g.  Phase changes were studied through in-situ x-ray diffraction and in-situ Raman characterizations.  The stable structure provides long life cycling performance, and the pseudocapacitance behavior also demonstrates its benefits to the rate capability.  Thus dual ion batteries based on Na chem. are very promising to find their applications in future.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref14" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b03648"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qin, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Offset Initial Sodium Loss to Improve Coulombic Efficiency and Stability of Sodium Dual-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Offset Initial Sodium Loss To Improve Coulombic Efficiency and Stability of Sodium Dual-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ma, Ruifang; Fan, Ling; Chen, Suhua; Wei, Zengxi; Yang, Yuhua; Yang, Hongguan; Qin, Yong; Lu, Bingan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">18</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">15751-15759</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium dual-ion batteries (NDIBs) are attracting extensive attention recently because of their low cost and abundant sodium resources.  However, the low capacity of the carbonaceous anode would reduce the energy d., and the formation of the solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) in the anode during the initial cycles will lead to large amt. consumption of Na+ in the electrolyte, which results in low Coulombic efficiency and inferior stability of the NDIBs.  To address these issues, a phosphorus-doped soft carbon (P-SC) anode combined with a presodiation process is developed to enhance the performance of the NDIBs.  The phosphorus atom doping could enhance the elec. cond. and further improve the sodium storage property.  On the other hand, an SEI could preform in the anode during the presodiation process; thus the anode has no need to consume large amts. of Na+ to form the SEI during the cycling of the NDIBs.  Consequently, the NDIBs with P-SC anode after the presodiation process exhibit high Coulombic efficiency (over 90%) and long cycle stability (81 mA h g-1 at 1000 mA g-1 after 900 cycles with capacity retention of 81.8%), far more superior to the unsodiated NDIBs.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The com.     </div><div class="casAbstract">Pine needles are used as the precursor material to prepare hard carbon.  Scanning electron microscopy, X-ray diffraction, and N2 adsorption-desorption tests are carried out to characterize the surface, crystal, and pore structure of the material.  The pine needle derived carbon (PNC) exhibits excellent Na-ion storage ability.  A dual-ion battery of PNC/graphite using a Na(+)-based organic electrolyte is constructed.  The batteries display outstanding electrochemical performance: a superior energy density (200 Wh kg(-1) at 131 W kg(-1)), high cut-off voltage (4.7 V), and outstanding cycling stability (87.2% retention after 1000 cycles).  In addition, the separate responses of the cathode and anode are investigated.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref18" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1002/celc.201801282"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cao, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chu, P.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical MoS2@N-Doped Carbon Hollow Spheres with Enhanced Performance in Sodium Dual-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zhongyu; Yang, Liwen; Xu, Guobao; Liu, Xiong; Wei, Xiaolin; Cao, Juexian; Chu, Paul K.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ChemElectroChem</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium dual-ion batteries (S-DIBs) are attracting increasing interest in large-scale elec. energy storage, owing to low-cost and abundant sodium resources and the crucial need to develop high-performance anode materials to spur the large-scale application of S-DIBs.  In this work, hierarchical hollow spheres assembled from interconnected few-layer MoS2 nanosheets with an N-doped carbon coating (designated as MoS2@NC HHSs) are designed and synthesized.  An S-DIBs full cell is fabricated with MoS2@NC HHSs as the anode, expanded graphite as the cathode, and 1.0 M NaPF6 in EC/DMC/EMC (1 : 1 : 1, vol. ratio) as the electrolyte.  The combined effects rendered by the ultrathin MoS2 subunits, hollow interior, and N-doped carbon coating not only promote the reaction kinetics and capacitive-controlled Na storage, but also guarantee outstanding mech. stability during Na+ intercalation/deintercalation.  The MoS2@NC HHSs-based S-DIBs deliver a high reversible capacity of 45 mAhg-1 at 2 Ag-1 and exhibit good cycling performance with a stable reversible capacity of 40 mAhg-1 and high coulombic efficiency beyond 90 % at 1 Ag-1 for 500 cycles.  The MoS2@NC HHSs have great potential in high-performance S-DIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref19" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2018.03.011"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cui, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Three-Dimensional Carbon Frameworks Enabling MoS<sub>2</sub> as Anode for Dual Ion Batteries with Superior Sodium Storage Properties</span>. <i>Energy Storage Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>15</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">22</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">30</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Origin of low sodium capacity in graphite and generally weak substrate binding of Na and Mg among alkali and alkaline earth metals</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yuanyue; Merinov, Boris V.; Goddard, William A., III</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences of the United States of America</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">National Academy of Sciences</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is well known that graphite has a low capacity for Na but a high capacity for other alkali metals.  The growing interest in alternative cation batteries beyond Li makes it particularly important to elucidate the origin of this behavior, which is not well understood.  In examg. this question, we find a quite general phenomenon: among the alkali and alk. earth metals, Na and Mg generally have the weakest chem. binding to a given substrate, compared with the other elements in the same column of the periodic table.  We demonstrate this with quantum mechanics calcns. for a wide range of substrate materials (not limited to C) covering a variety of structures and chem. compns.  The phenomenon arises from the competition between trends in the ionization energy and the ion-substrate coupling, down the columns of the periodic table.  Consequently, the cathodic voltage for Na and Mg is expected to be lower than those for other metals in the same column.  This generality provides a basis for analyzing the binding of alkali and alk. earth metal atoms over a broad range of systems.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref29" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1149/1.1393348"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stevens, D.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A graphite/TiO2 full cell was developed as a new safety energy storage system using a highly safety process.  The crystal structures of the anatase TiO2 electrode were studied with respect to the performance of the electrodes.  Due to the large anion intercalation into the graphite pos. electrode, the possible charging potential can be raised to around 5.3 V against the Li/Li+ electrode, which is a higher charging voltage than lithium-ion batteries (max. voltage is ∼4.3 V vs. Li/Li+).                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">On the use of activated carbon as a quasi-reference electrode in non-aqueous electrolyte solutions</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ruch, P. W.; Cericola, D.; Hahn, M.; Koetz, R.; Wokaun, A.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Electroanalytical Chemistry</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The application of high surface area activated C (a.c.) as a convenient quasi-ref. electrode (QRE) in nonaq. electrolyte solns. is evaluated.  By calibration against the ferrocene/ferrocenium ion redox system, the potential of the a.c. QRE studied in this work was found to lie close to +3 V vs. Li/Li+ for several nonaq. electrolyte solns. and to exhibit drifts of &lt;+1 mV/day at room temp. for certain electrolyte solns.  The a.c. QREs are thus proposed as suitable alternatives to other QREs with the distinct advantages that no addnl. ionic impurities are introduced into the electrochem. system under study, no potential-detg. redox system is required and the electrode potential is less influenced by changes in the concn. of redox-active species in the electrolyte soln.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref35" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1016/j.cej.2017.09.044"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yan, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">TiO<sub>2</sub>@C Nanosheets with Highly Exposed (001) Facets as a High-Capacity Anode for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">TiO2@C nanosheets with highly exposed (0 0 1) facets as a high-capacity anode for Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Qi; He, Hanna; Huang, Xiaobing; Yan, Jun; Tang, Yougen; Wang, Haiyan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Surface engineering plays a key role in enhancing the electrochem. performance for energy storage materials.  Herein, TiO2 nanosheets with highly exposed (0 0 1) facets are synthesized by a HF-induced hydrothermal process and TiO2@C composite is obtained by the following carbonation reaction of phenolic resin.  As indicated, TiO2 nanosheets are averagely 50 nm wide and 4 nm thick and a homogeneous and ultrathin C layer (3 nm) is coated on the nanosheets.  When used as an anode in Na-ion batteries, it delivers a high stable specific capacity of 264.9 mA-h g-1 after 100 cycles at 100 mA g-1 and maintains a considerable specific capacity of 92.9 mA-h g-1 after 4000 cycles even at a high c.d. of 5 A g-1.                         cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Remarkable Effect of Sodium Alginate Aqueous Binder on Anatase TiO2 as High-Performance Anode in Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ling, Liming; Bai, Ying; Wang, Zhaohua; Ni, Qiao; Chen, Guanghai; Zhou, Zhiming; Wu, Chuan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium alginate (SA) is investigated as the aq. binder to fabricate high-performance, low-cost, environmentally friendly, and durable TiO2 anodes in sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) for the first time.  Compared to the conventional polyvinylidene difluoride (PVDF) binder, electrodes using SA as the binder exhibit significant promotion of electrochem. performances.  The initial Coulombic efficiency is as high as 62% at 0.1 C.  A remarkable capacity of 180 mAh g-1 is achieved with no decay after 500 cycles at 1 C.  Even at 10 C (3.4 A g-1), it remains 82 mAh g-1 after 3600 cycles with approx. 100% Coulombic efficiency.  TiO2 electrodes with SA binder display less electrolyte decompn., fewer side reactions, high electrochem. reaction activity, effective suppression of polarization, and good electrode morphol., which is ascribed to the rich carboxylic groups, high Young's modulus, and good electrochem. stability of SA binder.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref38" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2014.05.121"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nie, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Flower-Like Hydrogenated TiO<sub>2</sub>(B) Nanostructures as Anode Materials for High-Performance Lithium Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flower-like hydrogenated TiO2(B) nanostructures as anode materials for high-performance lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Zhonghua; Zhou, Zhenfang; Nie, Sen; Wang, Honghu; Peng, Hongrui; Li, Guicun; Chen, Kezheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Flower-like hydrogenated TiO2(B) nanostructures have been synthesized by a facile solvothermal approach combined with hydrogenation treatment.  The obtained TiO2(B) nanostructures show uniform and hierarchical flower-like morphol. with a diam. of 124 ± 5 nm, which are further constructed by primary nanosheets with a thickness of 10 ± 1.2 nm.  The Ti3+ species and/or oxygen vacancies are well introduced into the structures of TiO2(B) after hydrogen redn., resulting in an enhancement in the electronic cond. (up to 2.79 × 10-3 S/cm) and the modified surface electrochem. activity.  When evaluated for lithium storage capacity, the hydrogenated TiO2(B) nanostructures exhibit enhanced electrochem. energy storage performances compared to the pristine TiO2(B) nanostructures, including high capacity (292.3 mA-h/g at 0.5C), excellent rate capability (179.6 mA-h/g at 10C), and good cyclic stability (98.4% capacity retention after 200 cycles at 10C).  The reasons for these improvements are explored in terms of the increased electronic cond. and the facilitation of lithium ion transport arising from the introduction of oxygen vacancies and the unique flower-like morphologies.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref39"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref39" class="refNumLink">39</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit39" data-doi="10.1021/jp2039256"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chou, S.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.-Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.-K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.-X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Rapid Synthesis of Li<sub>4</sub>Ti<sub>5</sub>O<sub>12</sub> Microspheres as Anode Materials and Its Binder Effect for Lithium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>J. The Li4Ti5O12 microspheres were characterized by x-ray diffraction, Brunauer-Emmett-Teller N2 adsorption, SEM, Raman spectroscopy, and TEM.  Na CM-cellulose (CMC) was also studied as a low-cost green binder.  The electrochem. tests, including const. current charge-discharge, cyclic voltammetry, and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy, demonstrated that the electrode using CMC as binder had better high-rate capability than the one with polyvinylidene fluoride (PVDF) binder.  The electrode using CMC and PVDF as binder had the same Li diffusion coeff.  The electrode using CMC as binder showed much lower charge transfer resistance, lower apparent activation energy, and lower apparent diffusion activation energy than for the electrode using PVDF as the binder.                 10.1021/acsnano.7b09177</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D12%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D3424-3435%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DJ.%2BTian%26author%3DD.%2BCao%26author%3DX.%2BZhou%26author%3DJ.%2BHu%26author%3DM.%2BHuang%26author%3DC.%2BLi%26title%3DHigh-Capacity%2BMg%25E2%2580%2593Organic%2BBatteries%2BBased%2Bon%2BNanostructured%2BRhodizonate%2BSalts%2BActivated%2Bby%2BMg%25E2%2580%2593Li%2BDual-Salt%2BElectrolyte%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.7b09177&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b09703&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.7b09177&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Capacity Mg-Organic Batteries Based on Nanostructured Rhodizonate Salts Activated by Mg-Li Dual-Salt Electrolyte</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Tian, Jing; Cao, Dunping; Zhou, Xuejun; Hu, Jiulin; Huang, Minsong; Li, Chilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3424-3435</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A Mg battery is a promising candidate for large-scale transportation and stationary energy storage due to the security, low cost, abundance, and high volumetric energy d. of a Mg anode.  But there are still some obstacles retarding the wide application of Mg batteries, including poor kinetics of Mg-ion transport in lattices and low theor. capacity in inorg. frameworks.  A Mg-Li dual-salt electrolyte enables kinetic activation by dominant intercalation of Li-ions instead of Mg-ions in cathode lattices without the compromise of a stable Mg anode process.  Here, we propose a Mg-org. battery based on a renewable rhodizonate salt (e.g., Na2C6O6) activated by a Mg-Li dual-salt electrolyte.  The nanostructured org. system can achieve a high reversible capacity of 350-400 mAh/g due to the existence of high-d. carbonyl groups (C=O) as redox sites.  Nanocryst. Na2C6O6 wired by reduced graphene oxide enables a high-rate performance of 200 and 175 mAh/g at 2.5 (5 C) and 5 A/g (10 C), resp., which also benefits from a high intrinsic diffusion coeff. (10-12-10-11 cm2/s) and pseudocapacitance contribution (&gt;60%) of Na2C6O6 for Li-Mg co-intercalation.  The suppressed exfoliation of C6O6 layers by a firmer non-Li pinning via Na-O-C or Mg-O-C and a dendrite-resistive Mg anode lead to a long-term cycling for ≥600 cycles.  Such an extraordinary capacity/rate performance endows the Mg-Na2C6O6 system with high energy and power densities up to 525 Wh/Kg and 4490 W/Kg (based on active cathode material), resp., exceeding the level of high-voltage insertion cathodes with typical inorg. structures.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref43" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2009.11.096"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rui, X. The partial conductivity and elec. mobility of Li are 1.5 × 10-4 Ω-1-cm-1 and 3 × 10-8 cm2-V-1-s-1, resp., at the same stoichiometry and temp.  Because of the very large values of the chem. diffusion coeff. and the fact that 3 mols of Li can react per mol of Sb, this system may be of interest for use in new types of secondary batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref49"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref49" class="refNumLink">49</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit49" data-doi="10.1039/C8CP06248J"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dang, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiao, X.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">CuO-Coated and Cu<sup>2+</sup>-doped Co-Modified P2-type Na<sub>2/3</sub>[Ni<sub>1/3</sub>Mn<sub>2/3</sub>]O<sub>2</sub> for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Phys. Transmission electron microscopy (TEM) images, TEM elemental line scan anal. and ex situ SEM images show that CuO has been successfully coated on the particle surface uniformly, and that this CuO layer effectively suppresses the exfoliation of the metal oxide layers and unfavorable side reactions.     <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7031-7042</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The incorporation of oxygen vacancies in anatase TiO2 has been studied as a promising way to accelerate the transport of electrons and Na+ ions, which is important for achieving excellent electrochem. properties for anatase TiO2.  However, wittingly introducing oxygen vacancies in anatase TiO2 for sodium-ion anodes by a facile and effective method is still a challenge.  In this work, we report an innovative method to introduce oxygen vacancies into the urchin-like N-doped carbon coated anatase TiO2 (NC-DTO) by a facile plasma treatment.  The superiorities of the oxygen vacancies combined with the conductive N-doped carbon coating enable the obtained NC-DTO of greatly improved sodium storage performance.  When served as the anode for sodium-ion batteries, the NC-DTO electrode shows superior electrochem. performance (capacity: 272 mA h g-1 at 0.25 C, capacity retention: 98.8% after 5000 cycles at 10 C, as well as ultrahigh capacity: 150 mA h g-1 at 15 C).  D. functional theory calcns. combined with exptl. results suggest that considerably improved sodium storage performance of NC-DTO is due to the enhanced electronic cond. from the N-doped carbon layer as well as narrowed band gap and lowered sodiation energy barrier from the introduction of oxygen vacancies.  This work highlights that introducing oxygen vacancies into TiO2 by plasma is a promising method to enhance the electrochem. property of TiO2, which also can be applied to different metal oxides for energy storage devices.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref55" class="refNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit55" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b03722"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bin, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tamirat, A. G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrasmall TiO<sub>2</sub>-Coated Reduced Graphene Oxide Composite as a High-Rate and Long-Cycle-Life Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">14818</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">14826</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.8b03722</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D10%26publication_year%3D2018%26pages%3D14818-14826%26journal%3DACS%2BAppl.%2BMater.%2BInterfaces%26author%3DY.%2BLiu%26author%3DJ.%2BLiu%26author%3DD.%2BBin%26author%3DM.%2BHou%26author%3DA.%2BG.%2BTamirat%26author%3DY.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BXia%26title%3DUltrasmall%2BTiO2-Coated%2BReduced%2BGraphene%2BOxide%2BComposite%2Bas%2Ba%2BHigh-Rate%2Band%2BLong-Cycle-Life%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsami.8b03722&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b09703&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsami.8b03722&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrasmall TiO2-Coated Reduced Graphene Oxide Composite as a High-Rate and Long-Cycle-Life Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yao; Liu, Jingyuan; Bin, Duan; Hou, Mengyan; Tamirat, Andebet Gedamu; Wang, Yonggang; Xia, Yongyao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14818-14826</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Because of the low cost and abundant nature of the Na element, Na-ion batteries (SIBs) are attracting extensive attention, and a variety of SIB cathode materials have been discovered.  However, the lack of high-performance anode materials is a major challenge of SIBs.  We synthesized ultrasmall TiO2-nanoparticle-coated reduced graphene oxide (TiO2@RGO) composites using a 1-pot hydrolysis method, which are then studied as anode materials for SIBs.  The morphol. of TiO2@RGO was characterized using transmission electron microscopy, indicating that the TiO2 nanospheres uniformly grow on the surface of the RGO nanosheet.  As-prepd. TiO2@RGO composites exhibited a promising electrochem. performance in terms of cycling stability and rate capability, esp. the initial cycle Coulombic efficiency of 60.7%, which is higher than that in previous reports.  The kinetics of the electrode reaction was studied by cyclic voltammetry.  The results indicate that the Na-ion intercalation/extn. behavior is not controlled by the semiinfinite diffusion process, which gives rise to an outstanding rate performance.  The electrochem. performance of TiO2@RGO composites in full cells, coupled with C-coated Na3V2(PO4)3 as the pos. material, was studied.  The discharge specific capacity was ≤117.2 mAh/g, and it remained at 84.6 mAh/g after 500 cycles under a c.d. of 2 A/g, which showed excellent cycling stability.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref56" class="refNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit56" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201705788"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xi, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Porous Nanosheets Constructed by Graphene-Coated, Interconnected TiO<sub>2</sub> Nanoparticles for Ultrafast Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Adv. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>30</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">1705788</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.201705788</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D30%26publication_year%3D2018%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26author%3DB.%2BLi%26author%3DB.%2BXi%26author%3DZ.%2BFeng%26author%3DY.%2BLin%26author%3DJ.%2BLiu%26author%3DJ.%2BFeng%26author%3DY.%2BQian%26author%3DS.%2BXiong%26title%3DHierarchical%2BPorous%2BNanosheets%2BConstructed%2Bby%2BGraphene-Coated%252C%2BInterconnected%2BTiO2%2BNanoparticles%2Bfor%2BUltrafast%2BSodium%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.201705788&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b09703&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.201705788&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="

Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Determination of Lithium Diffusion Coefficient and Reaction Mechanism into Ultra-Small Nanocrystalline SnO<sub>2</sub> Particles</span>. <i>J. Power Sources</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>419</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">229</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">236</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2019.02.052</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D419%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D229-236%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DG.%2BAli%26author%3DS.%2BA.%2BPatil%26author%3DS.%2BMehboob%26author%3DM.%2BAhmad%26author%3DH.%2BY.%2BHa%26author%3DH.-S.%2BKim%26author%3DK.%2BY.%2BChung%26title%3DDetermination%2Bof%2BLithium%2BDiffusion%2BCoefficient%2Band%2BReaction%2BMechanism%2Binto%2BUltra-Small%2BNanocrystalline%2BSnO2%2BParticles%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2019.02.052&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b09703&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2019.02.052&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit58R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">58</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Determination of lithium diffusion coefficient and reaction mechanism into ultra-small nanocrystalline SnO2 particles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ali, Ghulam; Patil, Supriya A.; Mehboob, Sheeraz; Ahmad, Mashkoor; Ha, Heung Yong; Kim, Hak-Sung; Chung, Kyung Yoon</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">419</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">229-236</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High-performance electrode materials for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) are urgently required to meet the requirement of the widespread use of energy storage devices from small-to large-scale applications.  In this regard, ultra-small nanocryst. SnO2 particles with a size of ∼3 nm are synthesized using a simple hydrothermal method and investigated as a high capacity anode material for LIBs.  The SnO2 anode shows a high reversible capacity of 1026 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 150 mA g-1.  The kinetic study of the anode material is conducted and compared using cyclic voltammetry, electrochem. impedance spectroscopy and galvanostatic intermittent titrn. techniques and the lithium diffusion coeff. at open circuit potential is calcd. to be 3.71978 × 10-13, 1.818 × 10-14, and ∼1.82 × 10-16 cm2 s-1, resp.  The reaction mechanism of highly reversible SnO2 nanoparticles is investigated using ex-situ XRD, XPS, in-situ X-ray absorption near edge spectroscopy, and TEM and the results reveal the formation of lithium-tin alloy in the lithiated electrode and reversible formation of SnO2 upon delithiation.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref59"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref59" class="refNumLink">59</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit59" data-doi="10.1039/C8NR08511K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shangguan, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Powder Exfoliated MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets with Highly Monolayer-Rich Structures as High-Performance Lithium-/Sodium-Ion-Battery Electrodes</span>. <i>Nanoscale</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1887</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1900</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C8NR08511K</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D11%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D1887-1900%26journal%3DNanoscale%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DK.%2BChang%26author%3DE.%2BShangguan%26author%3DD.%2BGuo%26author%3DW.%2BZhou%26author%3DY.%2BHou%26author%3DH.%2BTang%26author%3DB.%2BLi%26author%3DZ.%2BChang%26title%3DPowder%2BExfoliated%2BMoS2%2BNanosheets%2Bwith%2BHighly%2BMonolayer-Rich%2BStructures%2Bas%2BHigh-Performance%2BLithium-%252FSodium-Ion-Battery%2BElectrodes%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC8NR08511K&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.9b09703&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC8NR08511K&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Powder exfoliated MoS2 nanosheets with highly monolayer-rich structures as high-performance lithium-/sodium-ion-battery electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yihui; Chang, Kun; Shangguan, Enbo; Guo, Donglei; Zhou, Wei; Hou, Yan; Tang, Hongwei; Li, Bao; Chang, Zhaorong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1887-1900</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NANOHL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2040-3372</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to their low yield and easy aggregation during the electrode prepn. process, exfoliated MoS2 monolayers cannot fulfill the requirements of alkali-metal-ion battery tests.  Hence, we have developed a facile process to fabricate powder exfoliated MoS2 nanosheets capable of large-scale prodn. and having highly monolayer-rich structures.  This process contains two steps: liq.-phase exfoliation of the edge-rich MoS2 precursor and a freeze-drying procedure.  The proposed MoS2 precursors contain rich edge fractions that are easily exfoliated by this method, and the freeze-drying procedure can maintain the unique monolayer-rich structure of MoS2 in the powder phase.  The electrochem. evaluations of both lithium- and sodium-ion batteries reveal that the proposed powder exfoliated monolayer-rich MoS2 electrode exhibits remarkable specific capacities and stable cyclic performances.  In particular, the monolayer-rich MoS2 nanosheet electrode delivers a superior lithium-storage capacity of ∼1400 mA h g-1.  The exfoliated MoS2 nanosheet electrode can withstand over 1000 cycles even at 1 A g-1.  The mechanism reveals that these unique MoS2 nanosheets not only have a large surface area but also their inclusive monolayer structures exhibit much higher charge mobility than those of bulk MoS2.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript"     <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">While lithium-ion batteries dominate the field of high-energy-d. applications, a variety of promising alternative battery technologies exist that might be suitable for various application purposes.  Their requirements may vary considerably, e.g., for stationary batteries they are significantly different from those of traction batteries in elec. vehicles, i.e., low installation and lifetime cost and a long cycle life are the key parameters for the former ones.  Here, we review the recent developments of dual-ion battery (DIB) and particularly of dual-graphite battery technologies, which may be considered as sustainable option for grid storage.  We present the progress and challenges of DIB materials and electrolytes, esp. with respect to performance parameters, e.g., energy d. and cycling stability as well as cost.  We discuss the major challenges for practical application and critically evaluate the DIB technol. along with an assessment of the potential to fulfill the targets for grid storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2017.01.034"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Meister, P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fromm, O.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rothermel, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kasnatscheew, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Winter, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Placke, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium-Based vs. Lithium-Based Dual-Ion Cells: Electrochemical Study of Anion Intercalation/De-Intercalation into/from Graphite and Metal Plating/Dissolution Behavior</span>. <i>Electrochim. Acta</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>228</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">18</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">27</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2017.01.034</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium-Based vs. Lithium-Based Dual-Ion Cells: Electrochemical Study of Anion Intercalation/De-Intercalation into/from Graphite and Metal Plating/Dissolution Behavior</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Meister, Paul; Fromm, Olga; Rothermel, Sergej; Kasnatscheew, Johannes; Winter, Martin; Placke, Tobias</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">228</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">18-27</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Energy storage systems utilizing a simultaneous intercalation of anions into a graphite host structure at the pos. electrode and intercalation/insertion/redn. or deposition of cations at the neg. electrode during charge, were introduced under the term dual-ion cells, recently.  In this work, the electrochem. intercalation of TFSI- anions into graphite has been studied in sodium-based dual-ion cells (SDICs) at different upper cut-off potentials varying between 4.5-4.7 V vs. Na/Na+.  Electrochem. characteristics of SDICs, including the reversible capacity, Coulombic efficiency, energy efficiency and onset potentials for anion intercalation, were evaluated in comparison to the lithium-based dual-ions cells (LDICs).  A stable charge/discharge cycling performance over 500 cycles has been found for SDICs providing a specific capacity of ≈ 32 mAh g-1 and a Coulombic efficiency exceeding 99% at an upper cut-off potential of 4.7 V vs. Na/Na+ at the graphite cathode.  By the addn. of the electrolyte additive ethylene sulfite (ES), an increase of the reversible capacity to ≈ 46 mAh g-1 was achieved.  Furthermore, possible reasons for the overall inferior cycling performance in terms of capacity for SDICs as compared to LDICs such as an increased overpotential for plating/stripping of Na+ ions as compared to Li+ ions are discussed.  In this respect, it was also found that the addn. of ethylene sulfite particularly decreases the overpotentials for the metal plating process, which at least partially explains the enhanced reversible capacity in LDICs and SDICs by using ES as electrolyte additive.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2017.01.037"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Aladinli, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bordet, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ahlbrecht, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tübke, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Holzapfel, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Compositional Graphitic Cathode Investigation and Structural Characterization Tests for Na-Based Dual-Ion Battery Applications Using Ethylene Carbonate: Ethyl Methyl Carbonate-Based Electrolyte</span>. <i>Electrochim. Acta</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>228</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">503</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">512</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2017.01.037</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit6R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">6</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Compositional graphitic cathode investigation and structural characterization tests for Na-based dual-ion battery applications using ethylene carbonate:ethyl methyl carbonate-based electrolyte</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Aladinli, Sinan; Bordet, Francois; Ahlbrecht, Katharina; Tuebke, Jens; Holzapfel, Michael</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">228</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">503-512</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">As significant as the electrolyte selection is for dual-ion battery applications, the characteristics of the graphitic cathode can also be decisive for the resultant cell operation.  During this work, to find a promising electrode-electrolyte combination for Na-based dual-ion batteries, CCCV cycling tests were applied to different pos. electrode compns. to optimize the effects of carbon black and binder as well as to mitigate the irreversible charge losses, by utilizing 0.5 M NaPF6/EC:EMC electrolyte which was the most promising mixt. in our preceding study.  Electrodes consisting of 90% KS6 graphite, 2% carbon black and 8% binder was the most promising combination, and proved its superiority over SLP 30 type graphite, delivering 86.2 mAh/g discharge capacity by its lower particle size and larger surface area.  Moreover, structural characterization tests of Raman spectroscopy and x-ray diffraction were implemented by providing qual. and quant. insights to elucidate and characterize the PF-6 intercalation/de-intercalation characteristics for our Na-based dual-ion battery.  The results of the tests acknowledged that the surface and the bulk of the electrode behave differently.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref7" class="rightTabRefNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit7" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2017.02.041"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Aladinli, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bordet, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ahlbrecht, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tübke, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Holzapfel, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Anion Intercalation into a Graphite Cathode from Various Sodium-Based Electrolyte Mixtures for Dual-Ion Battery Applications</span>. <i>Electrochim. Acta</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>231</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">468</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">478</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.electacta.2017.02.041</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Anion intercalation into a graphite cathode from various sodium-based electrolyte mixtures for dual-ion battery applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Aladinli, Sinan; Bordet, Francois; Ahlbrecht, Katharina; Tuebke, Jens; Holzapfel, Michael</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">231</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">468-478</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ELCAAV</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0013-4686</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Electrolyte plays a crucial role for dual-ion batteries by supplying the ions to be intercalated into electrodes.  Yet, high operation potentials of such batteries limit the no. of suitable electrolytes to be used since they have to be stable upon cycling.  Here, sodium-based electrolytes were investigated by applying stability and cycling tests in order to observe their influences on anion intercalation behavior using graphitic cathodes.  Intercalation of PF-6 anions with org. carbonate solvents revealed relatively better discharge capacities compared to its anionic counterparts and 0.5 M NaPF6/EC:EMC electrolyte was found to be the most promising mixt. among them.  PC solvent proved detrimental for anion intercalation, but FEC as an electrolyte additive in PC precluded undesired effects of PC and gave rise to reversible cycling.  However, the ionic liqs. based on TFSI- and FSI- anions, mostly, yielded capacity fading under a charging end potential of 5.0 V vs.  Na/Na+, except the 0.7 M NaTFSI/Pip14TFSI electrolyte, showing 98% coulombic efficiency over 200 cycles.  During this work, electrochem. tests were conducted and evaluated to comprehend the impacts of electrolytes on the anion intercalation process.  EC:EMC-based electrolyte was then used in our further research, where the compositional cathodic investigation was executed and the anion intercalation phenomenon was characterized.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref8" class="rightTabRefNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit8" data-doi="10.1021/acs.jpcc.7b08429"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liao, H.-J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Y.-M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kao, Y.-T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">An, J.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lai, Y.-H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, D.-Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Freestanding Cathode Electrode Design for High-Performance Sodium Dual-Ion Battery</span>. <i>J. Phys. Chem. C</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>121</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">24463</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">24469</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.jpcc.7b08429</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Freestanding Cathode Electrode Design for High-Performance Sodium Dual-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liao, Hsiang-Ju; Chen, Yu-Mei; Kao, Yu-Ting; An, Ji-Yao; Lai, Ying-Huang; Wang, Di-Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">121</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">44</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">24463-24469</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCCCK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1932-7447</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, both advantages of sodium-ion batteries and dual-ion batteries have been combined in an innovated sodium-ion-based dual-ion battery (SDI) system using a Na metal film as anode and a freestanding meso-carbon microbead film (FS-MCMB) as cathode.  FS-MCMB in SDI battery exhibited a superior working performance with the specific capacity of 83.6 mAh/g and a remarkable long-term stability over 300 cycles.  The SDI battery with FS-MCMB exhibited an advantage of high mass d. loading in the range of 2-7.5 mg cm-2, which was equal to a comparable capacity of 78-83 mAh/g.  The electrochem. impedance anal. indicated that FS-MCMB provided a superior permeability, resulting in facilitating electrolyte infiltration into MCMB structure.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Dual-ion batteries operate on two intercalants: anions for the cathode and cations for the anode.  This battery was initially known as a dual-graphite battery, where both electrodes are graphitic carbon.  The primary challenge of dual-graphite batteries is the very high operation potential of the cathode, often requiring an upper cutoff potential above 5 V vs Li+/Li.  Such a potential readily oxidizes alkyl and alkylene carbonate-based electrolytes.  The anode side, in fact, can employ any anode of most metal-ion batteries, although, to date, the focus has still been the Li-graphite anode.  Recent progress has significantly advanced the technol. readiness level for this battery.  Additives or ionic liq. electrolytes help mitigate cathode irreversibility; nongraphite anodes, such as aluminum, allow new carbonate electrolytes that lack the necessity of ethylene carbonate; nongraphite cathodes, including metal-org. frameworks and polycyclic arom. hydrocarbons have exhibited a remarkable potential.  This Perspective highlights the challenges, summarizes the recent progress, and attempts to point out future directions in the field.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1002/advs.201700146"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ma, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Deng, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Dou, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Progress in Graphite Intercalation Compounds for Rechargeable Metal (Li, Na, K, Al)-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv. In this Progress Report, we briefly review the application of GICs as anodes and cathodes in metal (Li, Na, K, Al) ion batteries.
