        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium dual-ion batteries (NDIBs) are attracting extensive attention recently because of their low cost and abundant sodium resources.  However, the low capacity of the carbonaceous anode would reduce the energy d., and the formation of the solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) in the anode during the initial cycles will lead to large amt. consumption of Na+ in the electrolyte, which results in low Coulombic efficiency and inferior stability of the NDIBs.  To address these issues, a phosphorus-doped soft carbon (P-SC) anode combined with a presodiation process is developed to enhance the performance of the NDIBs.  The phosphorus atom doping could enhance the elec. cond. and further improve the sodium storage property.  On the other hand, an SEI could preform in the anode during the presodiation process; thus the anode has no need to consume large amts. of Na+ to form the SEI during the cycling of the NDIBs.  Consequently, the NDIBs with P-SC anode after the presodiation process exhibit high Coulombic efficiency (over 90%) and long cycle stability (81 mA h g-1 at 1000 mA g-1 after 900 cycles with capacity retention of 81.8%), far more superior to the unsodiated NDIBs.  This work may provide guidance for developing high performance NDIBs in the future.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref15" class="rightTabRefNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit15" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201602778"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fan, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, B.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Soft Carbon as Anode for High-Performance Sodium-Based Dual Ion Full Battery</span>. <i>Adv. The growing interest in alternative cation batteries beyond Li makes it particularly important to elucidate the origin of this behavior, which is not well understood.  In examg. this question, we find a quite general phenomenon: among the alkali and alk. earth metals, Na and Mg generally have the weakest chem. binding to a given substrate, compared with the other elements in the same column of the periodic table.  We demonstrate this with quantum mechanics calcns. for a wide range of substrate materials (not limited to C) covering a variety of structures and chem. compns.  The phenomenon arises from the competition between trends in the ionization energy and the ion-substrate coupling, down the columns of the periodic table.  Consequently, the cathodic voltage for Na and Mg is expected to be lower than those for other metals in the same column.  This generality provides a basis for analyzing the binding of alkali and alk. earth metal atoms over a broad range of systems.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref29" class="rightTabRefNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit29" data-doi="10.1149/1.1393348"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Stevens, D. When evaluated for lithium storage capacity, the hydrogenated TiO2(B) nanostructures exhibit enhanced electrochem. energy storage performances compared to the pristine TiO2(B) nanostructures, including high capacity (292.3 mA-h/g at 0.5C), excellent rate capability (179.6 mA-h/g at 10C), and good cyclic stability (98.4% capacity retention after 200 cycles at 10C).         </div><div class="casAbstract">A Mg battery is a promising candidate for large-scale transportation and stationary energy storage due to the security, low cost, abundance, and high volumetric energy d. of a Mg anode.  But there are still some obstacles retarding the wide application of Mg batteries, including poor kinetics of Mg-ion transport in lattices and low theor. capacity in inorg. frameworks.  A Mg-Li dual-salt electrolyte enables kinetic activation by dominant intercalation of Li-ions instead of Mg-ions in cathode lattices without the compromise of a stable Mg anode process.  Here, we propose a Mg-org. battery based on a renewable rhodizonate salt (e.g., Na2C6O6) activated by a Mg-Li dual-salt electrolyte.  The nanostructured org. system can achieve a high reversible capacity of 350-400 mAh/g due to the existence of high-d. carbonyl groups (C=O) as redox sites.  Nanocryst. Na2C6O6 wired by reduced graphene oxide enables a high-rate performance of 200 and 175 mAh/g at 2.5 (5 C) and 5 A/g (10 C), resp., which also benefits from a high intrinsic diffusion coeff. (10-12-10-11 cm2/s) and pseudocapacitance contribution (&gt;60%) of Na2C6O6 for Li-Mg co-intercalation.  The suppressed exfoliation of C6O6 layers by a firmer non-Li pinning via Na-O-C or Mg-O-C and a dendrite-resistive Mg anode lead to a long-term cycling for ≥600 cycles.  Such an extraordinary capacity/rate performance endows the Mg-Na2C6O6 system with high energy and power densities up to 525 Wh/Kg and 4490 W/Kg (based on active cathode material), resp., exceeding the level of high-voltage insertion cathodes with typical inorg. structures.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref43" class="rightTabRefNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit43" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2009.11.096"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rui, X.                 10.1021/acsami.7b13760</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit54R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">54</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Plasma-Induced Oxygen Vacancies in Urchin-Like Anatase Titania Coated by Carbon for Excellent Sodium-Ion Battery Anodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gan, Qingmeng; He, Hanna; Zhao, Kuangmin; He, Zhen; Liu, Suqin; Yang, Shuping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7031-7042</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The incorporation of oxygen vacancies in anatase TiO2 has been studied as a promising way to accelerate the transport of electrons and Na+ ions, which is important for achieving excellent electrochem. properties for anatase TiO2.  However, wittingly introducing oxygen vacancies in anatase TiO2 for sodium-ion anodes by a facile and effective method is still a challenge.  In this work, we report an innovative method to introduce oxygen vacancies into the urchin-like N-doped carbon coated anatase TiO2 (NC-DTO) by a facile plasma treatment.  The superiorities of the oxygen vacancies combined with the conductive N-doped carbon coating enable the obtained NC-DTO of greatly improved sodium storage performance.  When served as the anode for sodium-ion batteries, the NC-DTO electrode shows superior electrochem. performance (capacity: 272 mA h g-1 at 0.25 C, capacity retention: 98.8% after 5000 cycles at 10 C, as well as ultrahigh capacity: 150 mA h g-1 at 15 C).  D. functional theory calcns. combined with exptl. results suggest that considerably improved sodium storage performance of NC-DTO is due to the enhanced electronic cond. from the N-doped carbon layer as well as narrowed band gap and lowered sodiation energy barrier from the introduction of oxygen vacancies.  This work highlights that introducing oxygen vacancies into TiO2 by plasma is a promising method to enhance the electrochem. property of TiO2, which also can be applied to different metal oxides for energy storage devices.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref55" class="rightTabRefNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit55" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b03722"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Bin, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tamirat, A. G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xia, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Ultrasmall TiO<sub>2</sub>-Coated Reduced Graphene Oxide Composite as a High-Rate and Long-Cycle-Life Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">14818</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">14826</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsami.8b03722</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Ultrasmall TiO2-Coated Reduced Graphene Oxide Composite as a High-Rate and Long-Cycle-Life Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Yao; Liu, Jingyuan; Bin, Duan; Hou, Mengyan; Tamirat, Andebet Gedamu; Wang, Yonggang; Xia, Yongyao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">17</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">14818-14826</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Because of the low cost and abundant nature of the Na element, Na-ion batteries (SIBs) are attracting extensive attention, and a variety of SIB cathode materials have been discovered.  However, the lack of high-performance anode materials is a major challenge of SIBs.  We synthesized ultrasmall TiO2-nanoparticle-coated reduced graphene oxide (TiO2@RGO) composites using a 1-pot hydrolysis method, which are then studied as anode materials for SIBs.  The morphol. of TiO2@RGO was characterized using transmission electron microscopy, indicating that the TiO2 nanospheres uniformly grow on the surface of the RGO nanosheet.  As-prepd. TiO2@RGO composites exhibited a promising electrochem. performance in terms of cycling stability and rate capability, esp. the initial cycle Coulombic efficiency of 60.7%, which is higher than that in previous reports.  The kinetics of the electrode reaction was studied by cyclic voltammetry.  The results indicate that the Na-ion intercalation/extn. behavior is not controlled by the semiinfinite diffusion process, which gives rise to an outstanding rate performance.  The electrochem. performance of TiO2@RGO composites in full cells, coupled with C-coated Na3V2(PO4)3 as the pos. material, was studied.  The discharge specific capacity was ≤117.2 mAh/g, and it remained at 84.6 mAh/g after 500 cycles under a c.d. of 2 A/g, which showed excellent cycling stability.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref56"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref56" class="rightTabRefNumLink">56</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit56" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201705788"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xi, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lin, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qian, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xiong, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Porous Nanosheets Constructed by Graphene-Coated, Interconnected TiO<sub>2</sub> Nanoparticles for Ultrafast Sodium Storage</span>. <i>Adv. Mater.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>30</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">1705788</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.201705788</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref57" class="rightTabRefNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit57" data-doi="10.1002/smll.201704508"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Que, L.-F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, F.-D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.-B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gu, D.-M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Pseudocapacitance of TiO<sub>2–x</sub>/CNT Anodes for High-Performance Quasi-Solid-State Li-Ion and Na-Ion Capacitors</span>. <i>Small</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2018</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>14</i></span>, <span class="NLM_elocation-id">1704508</span> <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/smll.201704508</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref58"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref58" class="rightTabRefNumLink">58</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit58" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2019.02.052"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ali, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Patil, S. A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mehboob, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ahmad, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ha, H. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.-S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chung, K. Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Determination of Lithium Diffusion Coefficient and Reaction Mechanism into Ultra-Small Nanocrystalline SnO<sub>2</sub> Particles</span>. <i>J. Power Sources</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>419</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">229</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">236</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2019.02.052</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit58R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">58</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Determination of lithium diffusion coefficient and reaction mechanism into ultra-small nanocrystalline SnO2 particles</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ali, Ghulam; Patil, Supriya A.; Mehboob, Sheeraz; Ahmad, Mashkoor; Ha, Heung Yong; Kim, Hak-Sung; Chung, Kyung Yoon</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">419</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">229-236</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">High-performance electrode materials for lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) are urgently required to meet the requirement of the widespread use of energy storage devices from small-to large-scale applications.  In this regard, ultra-small nanocryst. SnO2 particles with a size of ∼3 nm are synthesized using a simple hydrothermal method and investigated as a high capacity anode material for LIBs.  The SnO2 anode shows a high reversible capacity of 1026 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 150 mA g-1.  The kinetic study of the anode material is conducted and compared using cyclic voltammetry, electrochem. impedance spectroscopy and galvanostatic intermittent titrn. techniques and the lithium diffusion coeff. at open circuit potential is calcd. to be 3.71978 × 10-13, 1.818 × 10-14, and ∼1.82 × 10-16 cm2 s-1, resp.  The reaction mechanism of highly reversible SnO2 nanoparticles is investigated using ex-situ XRD, XPS, in-situ X-ray absorption near edge spectroscopy, and TEM and the results reveal the formation of lithium-tin alloy in the lithiated electrode and reversible formation of SnO2 upon delithiation.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref59"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref59" class="rightTabRefNumLink">59</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit59" data-doi="10.1039/C8NR08511K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shangguan, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, Z.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Powder Exfoliated MoS<sub>2</sub> Nanosheets with Highly Monolayer-Rich Structures as High-Performance Lithium-/Sodium-Ion-Battery Electrodes</span>. <i>Nanoscale</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>11</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">1887</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">1900</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C8NR08511K</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit59R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">59</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Powder exfoliated MoS2 nanosheets with highly monolayer-rich structures as high-performance lithium-/sodium-ion-battery electrodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yihui; Chang, Kun; Shangguan, Enbo; Guo, Donglei; Zhou, Wei; Hou, Yan; Tang, Hongwei; Li, Bao; Chang, Zhaorong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">11</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1887-1900</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NANOHL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2040-3372</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Due to their low yield and easy aggregation during the electrode prepn. process, exfoliated MoS2 monolayers cannot fulfill the requirements of alkali-metal-ion battery tests.  Hence, we have developed a facile process to fabricate powder exfoliated MoS2 nanosheets capable of large-scale prodn. and having highly monolayer-rich structures.  This process contains two steps: liq.-phase exfoliation of the edge-rich MoS2 precursor and a freeze-drying procedure.  The proposed MoS2 precursors contain rich edge fractions that are easily exfoliated by this method, and the freeze-drying procedure can maintain the unique monolayer-rich structure of MoS2 in the powder phase.  The electrochem. evaluations of both lithium- and sodium-ion batteries reveal that the proposed powder exfoliated monolayer-rich MoS2 electrode exhibits remarkable specific capacities and stable cyclic performances.  In particular, the monolayer-rich MoS2 nanosheet electrode delivers a superior lithium-storage capacity of ∼1400 mA h g-1.  The exfoliated MoS2 nanosheet electrode can withstand over 1000 cycles even at 1 A g-1.  The mechanism reveals that these unique MoS2 nanosheets not only have a large surface area but also their inclusive monolayer structures exhibit much higher charge mobility than those of bulk MoS2.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i8">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.9b09703" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.9b09703</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">Na<sup>+</sup>-storage ability of the TiO<sub>2</sub> anode; Ragone plot of TiO<sub>2</sub>/graphite DIBs; GITT curves; chronoamperometry plots and the relationship of ln(<i>i</i>) and <i>t</i>; CV curves of TiO<sub>2</sub> with Li-ion batteries; table for fitting results of Nyqusit plots; and reference table for diffusion coefficient (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/suppl_file/am9b09703_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.9b09703/suppl_file/am9b09703_si_001.pdf">am9b09703_si_001.pdf (943.03 kb)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

        <script nonce="931889c22ede54b8-SJC">
(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="931889c22ede54b8-SJC">
document.addEventListener('DOMContentLoaded', function () {
    const modalContainer = document.querySelector('.my-main-container');

    // Function to show the modal
    function showModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'flex';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'block';
    }

    // Function to hide the modal when the close button is clicked
    function hideModal() {
        modalContainer.style.display = 'none';
        document.querySelector('.overlay').style.display = 'none';
    }

    // Hide the modal initially
    hideModal();

    // Function to handle clicks outside the modal
    function handleClickOutside(event) {
        // const modalContainer = document.querySelector(".my-main-container");
        // Check if the click target is not a child of the modal container
        if (!modalContainer.contains(event.target)) {
            hideModal();
        }
    }

    // Add a click event listener to the close button
    document
        .querySelector('.close-button')
        .addEventListener('click', hideModal);

    // Add a click event listener to the document to handle clicks outside the modal
    document.addEventListener('click', handleClickOutside);

    const screenHeight = window.innerHeight;
    function updateModalPosition() {
        const scrollY = window.scrollY;
        // console.log("scrollY= " + scrollY);
        // modalContainer.style.top = `${50 + scrollY}px`;
        modalContainer.style.top = `${scrollY + screenHeight / 2}px`;
        // console.log("new top= " + modalContainer.style.top);
    }

    // Update the modal position when the user scrolls
    window.addEventListener('scroll', updateModalPosition);

    // Initialize the modal position
    updateModalPosition();

    //---Cookie---
    // Function to set the cookie with a given name, value, and expiration time in days
    function setCookie(name, value, days) {
        var expires = '';
        if (days) {
            var date = new Date();
            date.setTime(date.getTime() + days * 24 * 60 * 60 * 1000);
            expires = '; expires=' + date.toUTCString();
            console.log(expires + 'this is expires dateUTC');
        }
        document.cookie = name + '=' + (value || '') + expires + '; path=/';
        // console.log("document.cookie is: " + document.cookie);
    }

    if (!document.cookie.includes('modalAd')) {
        // Show Modal
        showModal();

        // Set the cookie with the name "modalAd", value "true", and expiration of 3 day
        setCookie('modalAd', 'true', 3);
    } else {
        hideModal();
    }
});

</script>
<link rel="stylesheet" type="text/css" href="/pb-assets/smartgroup_ads/Modal-LeadGen-1691422642793.css">
            
        </div>

<script nonce="931889c22ede54b8-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

      function init() {
        setTimeout(function () {
          var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
          if (cookieExist) {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
            return false;
          } else {
            //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
            gdprMessage();

        $("#gdpr-message-modal").show();

      function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
          //Submit the form
          //Hide form
          if ($(".gdpr_err")) {
            $(".gdpr_err").hide();
          }

          $("#gdpr-message-content");

      function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
          return false;

      function validateEmail(email) {
        var re =
          /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
      }

      function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
      }

      function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + "=([^;]+)"));
        if (match) return match[1];
      }

      function hideForm() {
        //And set cookie
        $("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag("event", "GDPR Modal", {
          event_category: "Pubs GDPR",
          event_label: "GDPR Dismissal",
        });
      }

      return {
        init: init,
      };
    })();

        <script nonce="931889c22ede54b8-SJC">
var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>

    $.getJSON('https://extreme-ip-lookup.com/json/', function(data, status) {
            if ( status == 'success' ) {
                $.each(data, function(i, field){

                    cookie=status;

            //TODO send cookie val to the controller for logging
